  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_949f0976-fee9-415d-931a-04b72b8560c8'
      });

<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">It's worth reading. It really doesn't get very interesting until the last third of the book. The the wordplay of Murakami and the ideas he expresses m<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">It's worth reading. It really doesn't get very interesting until the last third of the book. The the wordplay of Murakami and the ideas he expresses make the book worth reading through to the end. Also there is an interesting ending.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>

<div id="review_65749301" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/65749301" />
    <a title="Dasha H" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2584065-dasha-h"><img alt="Dasha H" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1249132961p2/2584065.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/65749301?book_show_action=true">Aug 01, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dasha H" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dasha H" href="/user/show/2584065-dasha-h">Dasha H</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Murakami virgins</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2584065-dasha-h?shelf=2009">2009</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer65749301" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14683951479646030079"><p>Don't get me wrong, I don't think this is, by any chance, a bad book. My low rating can be easily explained by the fact that I've already read <i>too much</i> Murakami.</p> <br/><p>I used to like him quite a lot, but come on, doesn't he get tired of writing the same book over and over again? Let me show you the pattern. A simple guy who likes to 1.cook 2.listen to music/read books 3. think about the meaning of life meets an ordinary girl who turns out to be totally extraordinary, which gets her into trouble soon a</p></span>
  <span id="freeText14683951479646030079" style="display:none"><p>Don't get me wrong, I don't think this is, by any chance, a bad book. My low rating can be easily explained by the fact that I've already read <i>too much</i> Murakami.</p> <br /><p>I used to like him quite a lot, but come on, doesn't he get tired of writing the same book over and over again? Let me show you the pattern. A simple guy who likes to 1.cook 2.listen to music/read books 3. think about the meaning of life meets an ordinary girl who turns out to be totally extraordinary, which gets her into trouble soon after the guy falls for her. The guy tries to save her from <i>something</i>, predictably dark, but fails. The ending is usually bleak and confusing. Doesn't it all sound familiar to you, experienced Murakami-readers?</p><br /><p>So, if <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9557.Sputnik_Sweetheart" title="Sputnik Sweetheart by Haruki Murakami" rel="nofollow noopener">Sputnik Sweetheart</a> was the first Murakami book I'd ever read I'd most definitely be head over heels for it right now. But after <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10374.Hardboiled_Wonderland_and_the_End_of_the_World" title="Hardboiled Wonderland and the End of the World by Haruki Murakami" rel="nofollow noopener">Hardboiled Wonderland and the End of the World</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11297.Norwegian_Wood" title="Norwegian Wood by Haruki Murakami" rel="nofollow noopener">Norwegian Wood</a>,<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/4929.Kafka_on_the_Shore" title="Kafka on the Shore by Haruki Murakami" rel="nofollow noopener">Kafka on the Shore</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11275.The_Wind_Up_Bird_Chronicle" title="The Wind-Up Bird Chronicle by Haruki Murakami" rel="nofollow noopener">The Wind-up Bird Chronicle</a>, etc., <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9557.Sputnik_Sweetheart" title="Sputnik Sweetheart by Haruki Murakami" rel="nofollow noopener">Sputnik Sweetheart</a> just falls naturally into the plain old "more-of-the-same" category and never <i>moves</i> me like I expected.</p></span>
  <a data-text-id="14683951479646030079" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_550245364" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/550245364" />
    <a title="Scarlet" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3839903-scarlet"><img alt="Scarlet" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1556098025p2/3839903.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/550245364?book_show_action=true">Mar 02, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Scarlet" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Scarlet" href="/user/show/3839903-scarlet">Scarlet</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3839903-scarlet?shelf=it-stays-with-you">it-stays-with-you</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3839903-scarlet?shelf=magic-realism">magic-realism</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3839903-scarlet?shelf=for-my-future-library">for-my-future-library</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3839903-scarlet?shelf=japan">japan</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3839903-scarlet?shelf=translated-works">translated-works</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer550245364" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18015373091063525721"><blockquote>
  <i>"Reality was one step out of line, a cardigan with the buttons done up wrong."</i>
</blockquote><br/><br/>I have come to realise that reading a Murakami book is not quite an act of reading itself but an act of dreaming with your eyes open. What you see is a series of surreal images barely held together by threads of reason. What matters however, is the feeling these images leave you with; an aftertaste that lingers and intensifies even as the world within these pages turns stranger and more disconcerting; until what yo</span>
  <span id="freeText18015373091063525721" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>"Reality was one step out of line, a cardigan with the buttons done up wrong."</i>
</blockquote><br /><br />I have come to realise that reading a Murakami book is not quite an act of reading itself but an act of dreaming with your eyes open. What you see is a series of surreal images barely held together by threads of reason. What matters however, is the feeling these images leave you with; an aftertaste that lingers and intensifies even as the world within these pages turns stranger and more disconcerting; until what you associate with the book is not the story or the characters, but simply, <i>that feeling</i>.<br /><br /><i>Sputnik Sweetheart</i> would forever be linked in my mind with an aching kind of loneliness. Like losing something you thought you owned and then realising it was never really yours.<br /><br />Only three characters inhabit the landscape in this book. Each is either a victim of unrequited love or incapable of being in love. They listen, talk, nod along and at the end of the day, go back to their lonely lives and continue to love just the person who cannot love them back. Like sputniks orbiting each other but never getting closer.<br /><br />I believe what Murakami does is strip life of all flamboyance and expose how mundane it really is. How personal can a connection with a stranger be when some part of him/her will always be a mystery? We can know people, yet not <i>know</i> them. Is love simply a dream we see to avoid the reality of our lonely existence; each life in a separate orbit?<br /><br />Indeed, reality bites.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>"And it came to me then. That we were wonderful traveling companions but in the end no more than lonely lumps of metal in their own separate orbits. From far off they look like beautiful shooting stars, but in reality they're nothing more than prisons, where each of us is locked up alone, going nowhere. When the orbits of these two satellites of ours happened to cross paths, we could be together. Maybe even open our hearts to each other. But that was only for the briefest moment. In the next instant we'd be in absolute solitude. Until we burned up and became nothing."</i>
</blockquote> <br /><br />Go on. Dream a Murakami.</span>
  <a data-text-id="18015373091063525721" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2396508451" />
    <a title="Kenny" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1642452-kenny"><img alt="Kenny" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1472073986p2/1642452.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2396508451?book_show_action=true">Jul 14, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kenny" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kenny" href="/user/show/1642452-kenny">Kenny</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780375726057" href="/book/show/397165.Sputnik_Sweetheart">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1642452-kenny?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1642452-kenny?shelf=murakami">murakami</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1642452-kenny?shelf=%E6%97%A5%E6%9C%AC%E3%81%AE">日本の</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1642452-kenny?shelf=sr%C4%91an-says-so">srđan-says-so</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1642452-kenny?shelf=queer-lit">queer-lit</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2396508451" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1956283870270741514"><b><i>“I dream. Sometimes I think that's the only right thing to do.”</i> <br/>Sputnik Sweetheart ~~ Haruki Murakami</b><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1531721405i/25980014._SX540_.jpg' alt='1' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>As I've stated previously, my friend, Srdjan, is obsessed with Murakami. Srdjan is so passionate about Murakami's writing that it is infectious. We've had many discussions about Murakami, and he kept prodding me to read one of Murakami's novels. He suggested <b>Sputnik Sweetheart</b>, or as I call it, <b>
  <i>Lust and Longing in Japan</i>
</b>. So, I took up his challenge, & plunged into this, strange, magical, lyri</span>
  <span id="freeText1956283870270741514" style="display:none"><b><i>“I dream. Sometimes I think that's the only right thing to do.”</i> <br>Sputnik Sweetheart ~~ Haruki Murakami</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1531721405i/25980014._SX540_.jpg" alt="1" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>As I've stated previously, my friend, Srdjan, is obsessed with Murakami. Srdjan is so passionate about Murakami's writing that it is infectious. We've had many discussions about Murakami, and he kept prodding me to read one of Murakami's novels. He suggested <b>Sputnik Sweetheart</b>, or as I call it, <b>
  <i>Lust and Longing in Japan</i>
</b>. So, I took up his challenge, &amp; plunged into this, strange, magical, lyrical world. <br><br><b>Sputnik Sweetheart</b> is a novel of what could have been, what might have been, where worlds overlap, &amp; love can never quite be divorced from lust. In the world of K, Sumire, and Miu, sex is often mistaken for love. <b>Sputnik Sweetheart</b> is strangely haunting but oh so hard to describe; is it a tale of unreciprocated love, unrealized ambition, and desire, of always wanting more? Even with it being filled with unreciprocated love rather than love, it is also one of the most romantic books ever written. Yes, at it’s heart, <b>Sputnik Sweetheart</b> is a romance novel. Wait, <b>Sputnik Sweetheart</b> is a detective novel. Perhaps it's neither; perhaps I'm entirely wrong. Hmmm ... do any of us really know what a Murakami novel is about? Srdjan advised me not to overthink Murakami. Perhaps he's right ... or maybe he's not.<br><br>I'll admit it; I don't really know what <b>Sputnik Sweetheart</b> is about. What I can tell you, is that its themes are love, the loss of love, passion, the loss of passion, desire, &amp; the loss of desire. Are the events K relates real or a dream? The only thing I do know is <b>Sputnik Sweetheart</b> is a beautiful novel <br><br>Regardless of what <b>Sputnik Sweetheart</b> is about, Murakami has seduced me.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1531721405i/25980015._SY540_.jpg" alt="2" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="1956283870270741514" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2330318419" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2330318419" />
    <a title="Jim Fonseca" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6743601-jim-fonseca"><img alt="Jim Fonseca" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1397669173p2/6743601.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2330318419?book_show_action=true">Mar 17, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jim Fonseca" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jim Fonseca" href="/user/show/6743601-jim-fonseca">Jim Fonseca</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6743601-jim-fonseca?shelf=japanese-authors">japanese-authors</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2330318419" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3255019549409108562">My sixth Murakami.<br/><br/>About three-fourths of the way through the book the magical realism kicks in. We have a woman who has an experience where she sees herself “on the other side.” There is also a disappearing woman in a situation where it is impossible for her to disappear; a tiny Greek island -- no well to fall into; a tiny town only accessible by ferry; a drowned body would wash up. <br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1521294001i/25228531._SX540_.jpg' width='363' height='242' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>The story is told from the points of view of two young people: a male teacher and a female would-be author. He lov</span>
  <span id="freeText3255019549409108562" style="display:none">My sixth Murakami.<br><br>About three-fourths of the way through the book the magical realism kicks in. We have a woman who has an experience where she sees herself “on the other side.” There is also a disappearing woman in a situation where it is impossible for her to disappear; a tiny Greek island -- no well to fall into; a tiny town only accessible by ferry; a drowned body would wash up. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1521294001i/25228531._SX540_.jpg" width="363" height="242" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The story is told from the points of view of two young people: a male teacher and a female would-be author. He loves her, but she is in love with an older woman. This is why she writes: “On a day-to-day basis I use writing to figure out who I am.” And “In order for me to think about something, I have to first put it into writing.”<br><br>A couple of passages that I liked:<br><br>“Remove everything pointless from an imperfect life, and it’d lose even its imperfections.” <br><br>“She scrutinized me for a while, like I was some machine run by a heretofore unheard-of power source.” <br><br>It’s a good story. The structure of the book is a lot like that of Norwegian Wood. A young man loves a young woman but she is out of reach for some reason. There’s a lesbian sub-story in both books. The man also finds himself attracted to the older woman in each story. <br><br>Syros Island photo from fanpop.com <br></span>
  <a data-text-id="3255019549409108562" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3096096316" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3096096316" />
    <a title="Candi" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3639005-candi"><img alt="Candi" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1585187464p2/3639005.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3096096316?book_show_action=true">Jun 12, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Candi" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Candi" href="/user/show/3639005-candi">Candi</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/5766426-sputnik-sweetheart">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3639005-candi?shelf=asia">asia</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3639005-candi?shelf=translation">translation</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3639005-candi?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3639005-candi?shelf=magical-realism">magical-realism</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3639005-candi?shelf=contemporary-literary">contemporary-literary</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3096096316" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1320134969733561663"><i>“Being all alone is like the feeling you get when you stand at the mouth of a large river on a rainy evening and watch the water flow into the sea… I can’t really say why it’s such a lonely feeling to watch all the river water mix together with the seawater. But it really is.”</i><br/><br/>I hope that Haruki Murakami is a forgiving sort of guy. I’d like to apologize for abandoning him several years ago. I had picked up <i>Kafka on the Shore</i>, set it aside, and just like that never came back to Murakami again. I d</span>
  <span id="freeText1320134969733561663" style="display:none"><i>“Being all alone is like the feeling you get when you stand at the mouth of a large river on a rainy evening and watch the water flow into the sea… I can’t really say why it’s such a lonely feeling to watch all the river water mix together with the seawater. But it really is.”</i><br /><br />I hope that Haruki Murakami is a forgiving sort of guy. I’d like to apologize for abandoning him several years ago. I had picked up <i>Kafka on the Shore</i>, set it aside, and just like that never came back to Murakami again. I don’t know why; I’m a true believer in second chances. It’s not like me to just suddenly drop someone and never think of him or her ever again. Well, to be honest, I have thought of Murakami on occasion, but it took the encouraging nudge of a wise friend to finally convince me of another try. This time I fell in love.<br /><br /><i>“A story is not something of this world. A real story requires a kind of magical baptism to link the world on this side with the world on the other side.”</i><br /><br />I’ve never read anything quite like this. It was similar to the feeling I have when waking from the most beautiful and haunting dream. My heart is expanded, my heart aches. There’s a sense of something hard to capture, fleeting; it will disappear in an instant. What remains is a sort of impression that is nearly impossible to explain. You can’t really tell anyone about it coherently because it only really makes sense to you alone. It’s just something you “know” and something you feel. You can’t get it out of your head. Your greatest desire is to go back to sleep forever, to dream that dream over and over again.<br /><br /><i>“So what are people supposed to do if they want to avoid a collision (thud!) but still lie in the field, enjoying the clouds drifting by, listening to the grass grow—not thinking, in other words?... The answer is dreams. Dreaming on and on. Entering the world of dreams, and never coming out. Living in dreams for the rest of time.”</i><br /><br />Somehow, I need to convey what this story is about. It’s about a lot of things. Things we can all relate to, such as unrequited love, loneliness, loss, desire, friendship. There are three major characters – Sumire, Miu and the narrator, referred to simply as “K.” Yes, there’s a love triangle, but one that is wholly mesmerizing. Sumire and K are friends of the best sort. They are much like soul mates but missing a connection of intimacy on the physical level. But that’s not for a lack of wanting, at least on K’s part. <br /><br /><i>“We used to spend hours talking. We never got tired of talking, never ran out of topics—novels, the world, scenery, language. Our conversations were more open and intimate than any lovers’… I imagined how wonderful it would be if indeed we could be lovers. I longed for the warmth of her skin on mine.”</i><br /><br />One day Sumire falls in love. A trip to a Greek island with her new employer, Miu, turns this book into something so surreal, so compelling, that I couldn’t stop reading. Murakami’s use of magical realism is used flawlessly. Sometimes I want to head for the hills when I get a whiff of this element in a book, but here I was completely drawn to it. I don’t think Murakami could have gotten his point across to me quite so clearly without it. Here we are in a world surrounded by people, some with whom we are even the most intimate. Yet we are lone souls always just missing that most elemental of connections for which we yearn. People pass in and out of our lives. Are we destined to never make that most perfect bond? Or does there exist the one ephemeral moment in time when it is just possible that someone will come into our orbit, our world, and make that connection, leaving behind a piercing memory of something gained and lost? Just like that dream you woke up from that keeps nagging you at the back of your mind for all eternity. <br /><br /><i>“We each have a special something we can get only at a special time of our life. Like a small flame. A careful, fortunate few cherish that flame, nurture it, hold it as a torch to light their way. But once that flame goes out, it’s gone forever.”</i><br /><br />I’m completely sold on Murakami’s writing now. I went on to download a collection of his short stories right after finishing this novel. I’ve added more to my list. His writing is not extravagant, not overstated. Yet it’s lyrical, beautiful, and infused with a sense of unfulfilled longing. It truly resonated with this reader. <br /><br /><i>“I closed my eyes and listened carefully for the descendants of Sputnik, even now circling the earth, gravity their only tie to the planet. Lonely metal souls in the unimpeded darkness of space, they meet, pass each other, and part, never to meet again. No words passing between them. No promises to keep.”</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="1320134969733561663" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer10723231302596280768">This is my first time reading a Murakami novel. It was very good, and very weird. Either large sections are entirely metaphorical, or we've got some heavy unreliable narrator action going on. Honestly, either way or any combination of the 2 is totally fine with me; this book was beautifully written.<br/><br/>It was eerily similar to Christopher Priest's <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/106925.The_Affirmation' title='The Affirmation by Christopher Priest' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Affirmation</a> in themes and quite a few plot points.   <span id="freeText10723231302596280768" style="display:none">This is my first time reading a Murakami novel. It was very good, and very weird. Either large sections are entirely metaphorical, or we've got some heavy unreliable narrator action going on. Honestly, either way or any combination of the 2 is totally fine with me; this book was beautifully written.<br /><br />It was eerily similar to Christopher Priest's <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/106925.The_Affirmation" title="The Affirmation by Christopher Priest" rel="nofollow noopener">The Affirmation</a> in themes and quite a few plot points. <div id="review_1522536749" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1522536749" />
    <a title="Vessey" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30910845-vessey"><img alt="Vessey" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1511166278p2/30910845.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1522536749?book_show_action=true">Jan 23, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Vessey" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Vessey" href="/user/show/30910845-vessey">Vessey</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30910845-vessey?shelf=4-stars">4-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30910845-vessey?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30910845-vessey?shelf=romance">romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1522536749" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10193603345929333186">SPOILERS<br/><br/>She said: <b>I really wanted to see you. When I couldn’t see you any more, I realized that. It was as clear as if the planets all of a sudden lined up in a row for me. I really need you. You’re a part of me; I’m a part of you.</b><br/><br/>He thought: <b>We’re both looking at the same moon, in the same world. We’re connected to reality by the same line. All I have to do is quietly draw it towards me.</b><br/><br/>I might be doing a disservice to Haruki Murakami with my attitude, but the desperate romantic in me, romantic</span>
  <span id="freeText10193603345929333186" style="display:none">SPOILERS<br /><br />She said: <b>I really wanted to see you. When I couldn’t see you any more, I realized that. It was as clear as if the planets all of a sudden lined up in a row for me. I really need you. You’re a part of me; I’m a part of you.</b><br /><br />He thought: <b>We’re both looking at the same moon, in the same world. We’re connected to reality by the same line. All I have to do is quietly draw it towards me.</b><br /><br />I might be doing a disservice to Haruki Murakami with my attitude, but the desperate romantic in me, romantic in a fluffy and nausea causing way, cursed with unhealthily and unreasonably optimistic nature, just cannot help but seeing her words as a confession of the love he longs for so much and his thoughts as a belief in and acceptance of that love. Or, as someone who fears loneliness and understands it all too well, I can see it the other way. No one gets the kind of love they need and every one of the characters goes on suffering in the same closed circle, and in the end everything is the same and everyone is lonely and in pain. But I choose not to. <br /><br /><b>"Why do people have to be this lonely? What’s the point of it all? Millions of people in this world, all of them yearning, looking to others to satisfy them, yet isolating themselves. Why? Was the Earth put here just to nourish human loneliness?"</b> <br /><br />I think that it’s good for such a story as this one to have an equivocal, open for interpretation finale. I think that the choice it requires of us resembles the choice we might have to make when our own personal stories our concerned. Does others' loneliness (or lack of one) make our own more or less bearable? Or maybe it does both? To what extent and in what way loneliness/happiness is a choice? I think it challanges us to try understanding better the nature of our own state of mind, our life, our ways, our own view of the world.<br /><br />I wanted to write a real review, but so far I can’t. Yet, I did not want to leave the first Japanese novel I had ever read (and what a novel that was) without some acknowledgement before saying goodbye. I imagined that those four stars, while waiting for me to come up with the substantial review I dream of, would feel awfully lonely on their own. It was a very evocative novel, beautiful, touching, <i>real</i>. I will certainly come back to Haruki Murakami.<br /><br />Read count: 1<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="10193603345929333186" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_22984378" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/22984378" />
    <a title="Seth T." class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/160319-seth-t"><img alt="Seth T." src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1251915636p2/160319.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/22984378?book_show_action=true">May 26, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Seth T." class="user" itemprop="url" name="Seth T." href="/user/show/160319-seth-t">Seth T.</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780375411694" href="/book/show/45316.Sputnik_Sweetheart">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Anyone who enjoys Murakami's special brand of genius.</span></div>

        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer22984378" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4841356053257036158">After the excellent <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/4929.Kafka_on_the_Shore' title='Kafka on the Shore by Haruki Murakami' rel='nofollow noopener'>Kafka on the Shore</a> and the perhaps much better <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11275.The_Wind_up_Bird_Chronicle' title='The Wind-up Bird Chronicle by Haruki Murakami' rel='nofollow noopener'>Wind-Up Bird Chronicle</a>, I've been on something of a Murakami kick. I find his storytelling fascinating, both in device and in style. His use of the extraordinary-as-mundane is a tasty joy for me to indulge. Sputnik Sweetheart, while not as wonderful an experience as the two aforementioned works, was quite a bit of quick fun.<br/><br/>Thematically not dissimilar from <i>Wind-up Bird</i>, this short novel revels in questions of identity, conscious </span>
  <span id="freeText4841356053257036158" style="display:none">After the excellent <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/4929.Kafka_on_the_Shore" title="Kafka on the Shore by Haruki Murakami" rel="nofollow noopener">Kafka on the Shore</a> and the perhaps much better <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11275.The_Wind_up_Bird_Chronicle" title="The Wind-up Bird Chronicle by Haruki Murakami" rel="nofollow noopener">Wind-Up Bird Chronicle</a>, I've been on something of a Murakami kick. I find his storytelling fascinating, both in device and in style. His use of the extraordinary-as-mundane is a tasty joy for me to indulge. Sputnik Sweetheart, while not as wonderful an experience as the two aforementioned works, was quite a bit of quick fun.<br /><br />Thematically not dissimilar from <i>Wind-up Bird</i>, this short novel revels in questions of identity, conscious vs. subconscious, the real vs. hidden world, and the nature of sexuality. The book is lean and packed with Murakami-style mystery—that is, both mystery in the detective sense and mystery in something closer to a Pauline sense, a revelation that is baffling to those who don't get it and uncanny to those who do.<br /><br /><i>Sputnik Sweetheart</i> revolves around three characters: 1) the largely passive narrator, K, a thirty-year-old elementary school teacher and passionate reader who is madly in love with 2) Sumire, a former classmate of K's who dropped out of school to become a writer and who has fallen madly in love with 3) Miu (whom Sumire calls her "Sputnik Sweetheart"), a married woman who imports wine, has a hidden past, and holds no ability to care sexually for her husband, Sumire, or really any other creature. All three are tortured by their own lives and despite the plot involving Sumire's abrupt disappearance off a secluded Greek island (a la <i>L'Avventura</i>), the story is less about the disappearance and K's subsequent investigation, and more a discussion of who people are and what is it that both separates and binds humanity from and to itself.<br /><br /><i>Sputnik Sweetheart</i> is not the best I've read from Haruki Murakami, but it was certainly worthwhile and a book I hope to revisit in a few years.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4841356053257036158" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1127819" />
    <a title="Kelly Wondracek" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/81305-kelly-wondracek"><img alt="Kelly Wondracek" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1566099275p2/81305.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1127819?book_show_action=true">May 09, 2007</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kelly Wondracek" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kelly Wondracek" href="/user/show/81305-kelly-wondracek">Kelly Wondracek</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780375726057" href="/book/show/397165.Sputnik_Sweetheart">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/81305-kelly-wondracek?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/81305-kelly-wondracek?shelf=surrealism">surrealism</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/81305-kelly-wondracek?shelf=japanese">japanese</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1127819" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17224706396003453792">Why does Haruki Murakami hit the spot so well for me, and for thousands of other readers worldwide? There's a common element in all his works; it's a bridge of fantasy and reality that has just the right delicate balance. There's something about that balance that's so mesmerizing. You can connect with it on a level that you can’t in pure fantasy, and there’s enough of a disconnect from solid reality to leave you in wonder. Of all the other writers that have been categorized as magical realism th</span>
  <span id="freeText17224706396003453792" style="display:none">Why does Haruki Murakami hit the spot so well for me, and for thousands of other readers worldwide? There's a common element in all his works; it's a bridge of fantasy and reality that has just the right delicate balance. There's something about that balance that's so mesmerizing. You can connect with it on a level that you can’t in pure fantasy, and there’s enough of a disconnect from solid reality to leave you in wonder. Of all the other writers that have been categorized as magical realism that I’ve read, Murakami is the one who masters this style the finest.<br /><br />Sputnik Sweetheart is the type of book that I pick up from my nightstand a Saturday morning right after I wake up, and read it until the last page, sometime early in the afternoon. The voice, the prose, the mystery…it’s all AMAZING.<br /><br />It's a story of an unconventional love triangle between the narrator, a young woman he loves, and the woman she loves, who doesn't have a drive for anyone. Bizzare things happen when the two women (the younger is the personal assistant of the older) go overseas for business and end up extending their stay on a Greek Island. The novel explores the concept of the "other side"; in terms of language and writing, in terms of being.<br /></span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_90529171" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/90529171" />
    <a title="K.D. Absolutely" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2156200-k-d-absolutely"><img alt="K.D. Absolutely" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1471967140p2/2156200.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/90529171?book_show_action=true">Feb 20, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="K.D. Absolutely" class="user" itemprop="url" name="K.D. Absolutely" href="/user/show/2156200-k-d-absolutely">K.D. Absolutely</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780375726057" href="/book/show/397165.Sputnik_Sweetheart">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Ranee </span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to K.D. by: </span>
      1001 Books You Must Read Before You Die
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2156200-k-d-absolutely?shelf=1001-non-core">1001-non-core</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer90529171" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8784053334550323815">This is my 2nd novel by Haruki Murakami and just like <i>Kafka in the Shore</i>, this still amazed me. I even enjoyed this more than <i>Kafka</i>.<br/><br/>For me this is the <b>best unrequited tragic love story</b> I've read so far. As this is said to be the most openly emotional novel of Mr. Murakami, the prose is really haunting and the scenes are dreamy and surreal. Again, because Mr. Murakami uses a lot of metaphors and symbolisms, there can be layers of interpretations. I am not really fond of love stories (this just ha</span>
  <span id="freeText8784053334550323815" style="display:none">This is my 2nd novel by Haruki Murakami and just like <i>Kafka in the Shore</i>, this still amazed me. I even enjoyed this more than <i>Kafka</i>.<br /><br />For me this is the <b>best unrequited tragic love story</b> I've read so far. As this is said to be the most openly emotional novel of Mr. Murakami, the prose is really haunting and the scenes are dreamy and surreal. Again, because Mr. Murakami uses a lot of metaphors and symbolisms, there can be layers of interpretations. I am not really fond of love stories (this just happens to be part of 1001 Books You Must Read Before You Die), but I choose to see this novel as a story of a tangled triangle of uniquely unrequited loves.<br /><br />The narrator, a 25-year old teacher, <b>K</b> is in love with a 22-year old lesbian writer, <b>Sumire</b>. However, Sumire is in love with her boss, a 39-year old married businesswoman, <b>Miu</b>. Miu and Sumire, working as the former's personal secretaty, went on vacation in Greece as a side trip from a business trip in Italy. Sumire told Miu her feelings. Because of her past, Miu could not reciprocate Sumire's love. The latter disappeared "like a smoke." <br /><br />There are many nice heartfelt quotes but the one below is my favorite as this explains the title. Based on history, Sputnik 1 &amp; 2 were the first man-made satellites launched by USSR in 1957. In Sputnik 2, there was a dog Laika that becaume the first living being to leave the earth's atmosphere, but the satellites were never recovered.<br /><br />With Sumire writing and referring to her and Miu:<br /><blockquote>
  <i>"And it came to me then. That we were wonderful traveling companions but in the end no more than lonely lumps of metal in their own separate orbits. From far off they look like beautiful shooting stars, but in reality they're nothing more than prisons, where each of us is locked up alone, going nowhere. When the orbits of these two satellites of ours happened to cross paths, we could be together. Maybe even open our hearts to each other. But that was only for the briefest moment. In the next instant we'd be in absolute solitude. Until we burned up and became nothing."</i>
</blockquote><br /><br />The novel is easy to read and it took me less than a day to finish all the 210 pages. Especially towards the end, I had to stop several times as the writing is so good that I had to close my eyes and think of my own lost or unrequited loves I had in the past. <br /><br />My unsuspecting wife thought that my knee was hurting. </span>
  <a data-text-id="8784053334550323815" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_477965014" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/477965014" />
    <a title="B Schrodinger" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5448792-b-schrodinger"><img alt="B Schrodinger" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1572325701p2/5448792.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/477965014?book_show_action=true">Dec 14, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="B Schrodinger" class="user" itemprop="url" name="B Schrodinger" href="/user/show/5448792-b-schrodinger">B Schrodinger</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5448792-b-schrodinger?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5448792-b-schrodinger?shelf=japan">japan</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer477965014" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8358901628140213429"><b>I sat down to read ‘Sputnik Sweetheart’ the night David Bowie died.</b> <br/>It was a humid,still antipodean January night where you knew sleep would not come easily. My partner, less accomodating of the heat than I am, nevertheless went to bed around 11 leaving me to late night reading. Unusually for suburbia, the only sounds were the crickets chirping their mid-summer thrum, a white noise, innocuous and soothing. It was a sombre evening and so it, and I, felt Murakami-like. Lost. <br/><br/>‘Sputnik Sweetheart’ i</span>
  <span id="freeText8358901628140213429" style="display:none"><b>I sat down to read ‘Sputnik Sweetheart’ the night David Bowie died.</b> <br />It was a humid,still antipodean January night where you knew sleep would not come easily. My partner, less accomodating of the heat than I am, nevertheless went to bed around 11 leaving me to late night reading. Unusually for suburbia, the only sounds were the crickets chirping their mid-summer thrum, a white noise, innocuous and soothing. It was a sombre evening and so it, and I, felt Murakami-like. Lost. <br /><br />‘Sputnik Sweetheart’ is one of the few Murakami novels I had yet to read. Soon I would have no Murakami yet to discover, if you can ever discover any new Murakami after reading only one of his novels - each being part of a Venn diagram with a multitude of overlaps, much like my memory of the cover of ‘Colourless Tsukuru…’ <br /><br />As the night wore on I read of K, the typical Murakami protagonist, and his friend Sumira who he met at university. They shared a bond as they were both outsiders who read voraciously. Sumira was named after a character in a Mozart song, a beautiful song with what Samira felt were ugly lyrics. This irked her. Why would her mother name her after a character in an ugly story? Sumira meets Miu, a successful business woman, at a wedding and falls in love with her. Miu recognises something she likes in Sumira and asks her to come work with her.<br /><br />I had to admit to myself that Murakami could be likened to a broken record, constantly skipping and replaying the same themes, but when he produces something so beautiful, you can forgive repetition. Miu argues that although they lyrics of Sumira’s song are ugly, the song is still beautiful and she should look past her feelings for the lyrics, just like I look past the broken record-ness of Murakami. <br /><br />When Miu phones K in a panic during the night I looked across at the phone near me. I half expected it to ring. But instead it just displayed the time,1:15. <br /><br />My partner woke a little later as K was travelling. She came out for some water, her eyes screwed up against the light, her hair fuzzy (don’t tell her I said that), and pillow-creases on her face. This look always made me smile. I hardly got to see it with her being an early-riser and me a night owl. She asked if I was okay and I told her I was. I asked if the music was bothering her. She said it wasn’t and urged me not to get too down listening to Bowie all night. And with that she retreated, my own little Sputnik. I was still awake, no chance of sleep.<br /><br />As I read Sumira’s writing Christmas beetles (<i>Anoplognathus pallidicollis</i>) were tapping on the window. They had found a light source and were endlessley and confusedly running into the glass barrier between themselves and the light. Sumira had been unable to write for so long. And now a breakthrough. But not for the poor beetles. <br /><br />As K came home again, alone and lonely, I did not feel lonely. The tortoise-shell cat went by on the fence outside on her night time and humanless adventures. She saw me through the open window and meowed asking “Why are you awake during <i>my</i> time?” But soon she was gone and K was back to his job as a teacher. Living his life one day at a time. <br /><br />And I was done. 2:56. I closed the book and looked up thinking of K and the phone rang. Who could it be at this time of night?</span>
  <a data-text-id="8358901628140213429" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_132327522" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/132327522" />
    <a title="Daniel Clausen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/957634-daniel-clausen"><img alt="Daniel Clausen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603533755p2/957634.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/132327522?book_show_action=true">Nov 25, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Daniel Clausen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Daniel Clausen" href="/user/show/957634-daniel-clausen">Daniel Clausen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/957634-daniel-clausen?shelf=top-books">top-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/957634-daniel-clausen?shelf=books-of-2018">books-of-2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/957634-daniel-clausen?shelf=books-of-2019">books-of-2019</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer132327522" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7459138701972172111">Reading Sputnik Sweetheart is like returning home. As the saying goes, you can't step in the same river twice...you can go home, but the home isn't the same home that you left. So it is with books. You can read the same words again and again, but since you are different, the book is different too. <br/><br/>This time, as I read this book, I dwelled on the topic of lost things. <br/><br/>"I closed my eyes and tried to bring to mind as many beautiful lost things as I could. Drawing them closer, holding on to them. Kn</span>
  <span id="freeText7459138701972172111" style="display:none">Reading Sputnik Sweetheart is like returning home. As the saying goes, you can't step in the same river twice...you can go home, but the home isn't the same home that you left. So it is with books. You can read the same words again and again, but since you are different, the book is different too. <br /><br />This time, as I read this book, I dwelled on the topic of lost things. <br /><br />"I closed my eyes and tried to bring to mind as many beautiful lost things as I could. Drawing them closer, holding on to them. Knowing all the while that their lives are fleeting." <br /><br />Reading this book, I couldn't help but think of all the lost things in my life. Great people and influences in my life that have moved away or moved on. They're not like books, stationary objects with fixed text. People really do disappear, though often in mundane ways. And it's hard to find them because mundane distances can be as bad and as troublesome as magical ones.<br /><br />How many Sumires have I known in my life? No less than four I would say. None of them vanished like smoke, and yet they are far away somehow. <br /><br />Like a Beatnik (Sputnik) writer, I return to this review looking for the portal. There is an island somewhere where all of the Sumires in my life still live. They are there waiting for me. <br /><br />My phone rings. <br /><br />"Hello." <br /><br />"It's me." <br /><br />I know the voice. It's not from one of the Sumires I lost, but from one of the Sumires I have not yet found. <br /><br />"Come find me." <br /><br />"But how..."<br /><br />"No more questions. You know what you have to do." <br /><br />Abruptly the phone cuts off. <br /><br />I need to cut the throat of a dog. I need to spill blood...no, no, that was how the novel went. But I am different. I don't need to spill blood. Spilling blood was only a metaphor anyway. <br /><br />I think about all the lost Sumires in my life. I open the book one more time. <br /><br />"In the spring of her twenty-second year, Sumire fell in love for the first time in her life. An intense love, a veritable tornado sweeping across the plains—flattening everything in its path..."<br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="7459138701972172111" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1115738404" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1115738404" />
    <a title="Helene Jeppesen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/21992464-helene-jeppesen"><img alt="Helene Jeppesen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528006866p2/21992464.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1115738404?book_show_action=true">Feb 22, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Helene Jeppesen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Helene Jeppesen" href="/user/show/21992464-helene-jeppesen">Helene Jeppesen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1115738404" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1548632857133597251">This turned out to be quite an interesting read. For the most part, I was utterly bored when reading this book. It contains long passages of bland thoughts and descriptions, and I was starting to think that I had grown away from Haruki Murakami and his story-telling which I used to absolutely love (I have read quite a lot of his novels through the years). <br/>However, halfway through the novel I encountered what was to become one of my favourite literary scenes (it contains a ferris wheel), and from</span>
  <span id="freeText1548632857133597251" style="display:none">This turned out to be quite an interesting read. For the most part, I was utterly bored when reading this book. It contains long passages of bland thoughts and descriptions, and I was starting to think that I had grown away from Haruki Murakami and his story-telling which I used to absolutely love (I have read quite a lot of his novels through the years). <br />However, halfway through the novel I encountered what was to become one of my favourite literary scenes (it contains a ferris wheel), and from then onwards the book picked up and caught my attention. For that reason, my rating is an average one. "Sputnik Sweethearts" contains - in my humble opinion - bland story-telling that is hard to get through combined with hugely interesting passages and thoughts on life mixed with some magical realism (as one can only expect from Murakami). In the end, I quite liked this novel, even though it isn't my favourite of his. </span>
  <a data-text-id="1548632857133597251" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_9678796" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/9678796" />
    <a title="Mariel" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/647547-mariel"><img alt="Mariel" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1451321467p2/647547.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/9678796?book_show_action=true">Nov 28, 2007</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mariel" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mariel" href="/user/show/647547-mariel">Mariel</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780375726057" href="/book/show/397165.Sputnik_Sweetheart">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Laika is my dawg</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Mariel by: </span>
      Be my 3am valentine
  </div>


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer9678796" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer821813328478122332">A moment in my life that has come back to haunt me during times of communication difficulty is when I told my grandmother that I hated to repeatedly shout out what I'd said for my mostly deaf grandfather because it made what I'd said sound stupid. Her response was that it was stupid all along, or something like that.<br/>I've decided that reading translated works and translating them again with one's mind, experiences, what have you is like doing a cover song. Jeff Buckley actually used another Leona</span>
  <span id="freeText821813328478122332" style="display:none">A moment in my life that has come back to haunt me during times of communication difficulty is when I told my grandmother that I hated to repeatedly shout out what I'd said for my mostly deaf grandfather because it made what I'd said sound stupid. Her response was that it was stupid all along, or something like that.<br />I've decided that reading translated works and translating them again with one's mind, experiences, what have you is like doing a cover song. Jeff Buckley actually used another Leonard Cohen song in his working of Cohen's Hallelujah. (I can't remember which one off the top of my head. This is going to bug me.) (Tv shows need to be more original. They can't use any other song?! My favorite Homicide: Life on the Street did it first, at least.) I mix up Murakami books in my mind. I'm not entirely sure that my favorite remembered things about Sputnik Sweetheart were actually in this particular book.<br />The wish to have someone you could call up at three in the morning and talk about anything you wanted. Even if they were asleep.<br /><a href="http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=C-Naa1HXeDQ" rel="nofollow noopener">Noooo, that's not what I meant!</a> Leave me alone, Rob!<br />Maybe I wouldn't like this book if I reread it. It's sorta caught in my mind of my ex. Speaking of Cohen, my ex hated him because he sang about being alone and yet always had lots of women. It smacked of "No one loves ME" resentment, which kinda sucked hearing from the guy you were with. (He wouldn't be satisfied with anything less than total world love.) Anyway, the narrator reminded me of him. I might hate that now... That's one problem that I do have with Murakami. His strength of seeing the sinister possibility or shadows of something that was always there is also too everyman at times when it comes to things like relationships. Like there are SUPPOSED to be these set rules that everybody follows with men and women. Or I could be remembering it wrong. We're not supposed to be anyone else. That's the beautiful thing about not always understanding what the hell anyone means. I dislike the general male-y everymanly things.<br />Still would want to talk at 3 a.m with the imaginary person who might actually get it and not care if they didn't.... (Shit. That fucking song is in my head now.)<br />I loved the description that the girl looked like she'd grow a beard if she could. I love descriptions like that 'cause that speaks to my brain functions in a way I can actually picture it. I think it was Murakami's Hard Boiled Wonderland and the End of the World that described the chick as looking good like playing a best friend of the lead in a movie. (The Flight of the Conchords did it even better. "You could be a part time model!")<br />My favorite part is the girl who splits into two people. That feeling lived in my eyes right off the pages.<br />You know what I really hate more than just about anything? Anyone who will respond to heart ache with a tale about how someone else has it worse (my ex EXcelled at this) like that means you should shut up. These people are always the ones who whine about the small shit, spare no self-pity. Whatever. I pretty much think those people should fuck off. If there's an everymanliness about the sex stuff (I didn't care if it was amazing to find a big girl hot, for example. Wonderland? I think?), Murakami is wonderful about the heart aches that matter because those are the beats you can hear pounding in your ears, no matter what else (shit talk) is drowning out the rest.<br />I wish I could read braille. I wonder what it would be like to translate words into finger touches.</span>

<div id="review_3073449451" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3073449451" />
    <a title="Reading_ Tam_ Ishly" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/102159719-reading-tam-ishly"><img alt="Reading_ Tam_ Ishly" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1578580640p2/102159719.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3073449451?book_show_action=true">Apr 10, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Reading_ Tam_ Ishly" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Reading_ Tam_ Ishly" href="/user/show/102159719-reading-tam-ishly">Reading_ Tam_ Ishly</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3073449451" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3215229087666041851">This first half of the book gave me equal satisfaction as The Seven Husbands of Evelyn Hugo by Taylor Jenkins Reid.<br/>But I thought the second part was really ridiculous.<br/><br/>Murakami's writing is different in the sense that this one is a little mainstream compared to his other novels. Nevertheless this book is so charming. The characters are so realistic and character development is so damn amazing.<br/><br/>It's the writing. Yes, his writing. It seems really simple but I have not come across many authors who wo</span>
  <span id="freeText3215229087666041851" style="display:none">This first half of the book gave me equal satisfaction as The Seven Husbands of Evelyn Hugo by Taylor Jenkins Reid.<br />But I thought the second part was really ridiculous.<br /><br />Murakami's writing is different in the sense that this one is a little mainstream compared to his other novels. Nevertheless this book is so charming. The characters are so realistic and character development is so damn amazing.<br /><br />It's the writing. Yes, his writing. It seems really simple but I have not come across many authors who would express as exactly as what we feel. It's like reading the mirror of your thoughts, feelings and emotions (the narrator's chapters are the highlights of this book).<br /><br />I changed my mind (previously I rated it 4/5 🌟). I cannot rate this book any lower. Because at many levels, I can relate so much with this book. <br />If words and writing can be as realistic as it can to a point that it is so enjoyable, you just cannot do anything else but keep on reading a Murakami book.<br />As a matter of fact, the characters hit home. As unpleasant and real as it sounds, two of these characters remind me so much of reality. (Moments after reading the book got me a bit high and hence the faulty rating. I needed to calm down and think about the book and decide what it made me feel in real.)<br /><br />The first half of the book mesmerized me. It's the second half that ruined the book. <br /><br /><br />And it's practically impossible to write a proper review for one of his books. Because it's all related to how real the writing gets while you're reading his books. <br /><br />This book is a good representation of queer, age gap relationship; a seeming author who keeps on writing; a narrator as real as one can get. It's about life in general and the longing of the possible love which would never be returned.<br /><br />*Some memorable lines:<br /><br />📌 He wasn't a talkative man to begin with, and in all aspects of life - like they were some kind of mouth infection he wanted to avoid catching - he never talked about his feelings.<br /><br />📌 Sumire was living in a one-room apartment in Kichijoji where she made do with the minimum amount of furniture and the maximum number of books.<br /><br />📌 A short girl beside me leaned over, took a look at the book, and asked me, Why Nizan, of all people? She sounded like she was trying to pick a fight. Like she wanted to kick something and send it flying but lacking anything suitable attacked my choice of reading material.<br /><br />📌 Devouring books came naturally to us as breathing. Every spare moment we'd settle down in some quiet corner, endlessly turning page after page. <br /><br />📌 Japanese novels, foreign novels, new works, classics, avant-garde to bestseller - as long as there was something intellectually stimulating in a book, we'd read it. <br /><br />📌 I'd never run across anyone else who read so avidly - so deeply, so widely - as Sumire, and I'm sure she felt the same. <br /><br />📌 It is the same with anything - you have to learn through your own experience, paying your own way. You can't learn it from a book.<br /><br />📌 I brewed a fresh pot of coffee, pulled a chair over next to the window, and sat there, munching on cheese and crackers. I sat, reading, waiting for the dawn. <br /><br />📌📌📌 The upshot of all this was that when I was young I began to draw an invisible boundary between myself and other people. No matter who I was dealing with, I maintained a set distance, carefully monitoring the person's attitude so that they wouldn't get any closer. I didn't easily swallow what other people told me. My only passions were books and music. As you might guess, I led a lonely life. <br /><br />(📌 Okay, I will stop. Otherwise half of the book will be here🤦)<br /><br />After thinking over the book over and over again for about 5 hours, I finally rated the book 3 🌟 because of the later half of the book. It was like Murakami was running out of ideas on how to finish up this book. It felt like the story turned into something that is somehow disconnected from the first half even though the three characters' lives were discussed. But it was like it was totally not required at all. The book ended up as just one average read. The ending was so rushed up where it mattered while a few unnecessary long chapters got pushed in between. <br /><br />But the first half was really good. The entire rating goes to that. <br /><br />I dive into Murakami's books blindly. No overhyping or underhyping play a part in my reviews when it comes to Murakami's book reviews.</span>
